RATING: 6.5
If I were a train game fan specifically this is probably near the pinnacle for anyone seeking a grind stone to press the brain on that's train oriented. It gets a lower rating for me personally as I like all games but am not specifically a train game fan. So some other game types/mechanics offering a similar level of brain drain will get played more at our table. A long game for sure, in the 2-3+ hour range depending on your table's chop chop level. Extremely low luck factor means you'll only have yourself to blame when it's going south, but that's kind of the hall mark of serious games for serious gamers anyway. If you like this zone of game play difficulty and like train games this is likely a must have for your collection. However I do warn that it's a long game and it's rules can be a bit arduous. At 5 or more players this can be a grindy game to trudge through.

RATING: 6.5
Very good pick-up-and-deliver train game. There is much interaction on the map, but also about who gets to deliver cubes first. Blocking of connections can become very mean. 

I do not like that there is quite some AP potential, when you try to determine which delivery gives you the most points, but which other delivery could give your opponent many points, and so on. 

I like Steam more than Railways of the World (or Railroad Tycoon), since I prefer the role selection to the cards. I also think that constructing railways is superior in steam, since the tracktiles with crossings and this little towns offer much more variety. The maps are also better balanced.

Update: After my third game I have to come to the conclusion that Steam is a bit too exhausting for me. This looking at the board and searching for optimal ways to transport cubes and looking for the best cube to move is more work than fun. It is also a bit repetitive. The game is still good and very interactive, but not an outstanding game to me.

RATING: 9.1
On it's own merits, Steam is an extremely good game. Streamlined, efficient, pleasantly heavy, and plenty of fun. 

As for the new elements, I like most of them as much or better than their previous implementations. I like the split victory/income tracks without the income reduction. I like having the option of playing a quicker game without an auction, the flexibility of the loan system, and the less random (though more chaotic) way that cubes are introduced onto the board. I generally like when choices like this are given to the players instead of to dice. 

All the elements work very well; it is balanced, quick playing with plenty of tough decisions both tactical and strategic. This is what I would have rated it if Age of Steam never existed.

RATING: 7
 Overall a good game. Plays smooth, the dichotomy between scoring and economy gives the game a nice transition between two different phases. At first looking to buildup the infrastructure while keeping you economy working, that progress towards a scoring race. There are plenty of opportunities for player interaction.

 Unfortunately there are some rough edges. First, the Germany map doesn't provide any kind of interesting choices. It's mostly a big plain with some rivers, without choke points that would allow deep strategical choices. That stresses another problem: the rail network can became so intrincate that turn some phases into an analysis paralysis slowdown. The US map geography conversely reduces that problem to some extent. Another big problem is the scoring system, current player score is completely open, so in the lasts turns kingmaking became an real issue as players that cannot win are conditioned in their decisions.

 It also features one of the worst ever rulebooks I have ever seen. Sixteen pages that shouldn't have been more than 4-5 at most, incredibly redundant and incomplete.

RATING: 8
Wow, we liked it more than we thought we would, after hearing how it was some devolved version of Age of Steam. We played with the full AoS style auction system. The chance-free production system seems better! The tile-laying costs do seem more elegant, once Petr pointed out the unifying logic behind them.

However we found the hieroglyphic role tiles to be annoying and hard to get used to, and the map's naturalistic art is prettier but provably less functional (as Macike got confused over whether a certain hex was mountain or not). Nice that it comes with 2 standard maps instead of 1. Need to play some more.

I have read various of the criticisms, and some seem valid:

1. Steam is more tactical and has less long-term planning because of the new production rules.
2. Steam's urbanization may be too powerful.
3. Issuing shares seems less costly, and possibly creates a runaway leader problem as a result of the ability to keep raising cash by issue shares once you're out of the hole and always win the auction while other players struggle to have cash.
4. The split VP/income tracks means whoever starts earning VPs first will probably win the game, and that ultimately only the final runs matter for victory. In AoS all of your runs have some direct effect on your score in the end.
5. Points for links instead of track removes minor tactics of building more track for points, using engineer, and urbanizing to cost someone track points. It seems done only to save time in scoring.

Maybe the best option is simply to play AoS with insta-production like from the London map?
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This game seems to hit all of the right spots for me.  You need to employ long-term strategic planning as well as tactical maneuvering.  Luck plays a factor but in the good way where it impacts all players equally.  A building game where you get to sit back and admire the empire you have built.  A great game that the whole family enjoys.

RATING: 10
This is a beautiful yet very tense game. You start off building simple connections just to ensure you recuperate your expenses. You ramp up throughout the game by building longer networks which in turn allow you to ship goods further for an even greater reward. The game is tense as you have to decide upfront how much money you need to bid and build tracks. Depending on the outcome of the bidding, you may not even be able to do what you had planned for. Always be prepared for plan B or C or .... I love this game.

RATING: 8
I'm not a big fan of train games, but this is the one I like the best. Actually, I think I like it quite a bit. The board is very neat with all the levels and income for all to see. All the usual aspects of the Age of Steam genre are simplified here.

Income and loans reminds me of the simplicity of Brass, rather than the fiddling around you have with Age of Industry.

The best improvement is the goods supply track replacing the blind drawing from the bag during the game. Out the window is the annoying uncertainty and luck of pulling cubes from the bag that might benefit your opponents more than yourself. Now you can plan ahead looking at the available groups of cubes. It adds an extra consideration to plan ahead for - in a good way.

Action tiles remind me of Automobile - a significant little bonus/benefit here and there that impacts upon your turn order in the next round.

I quite like playing this.

RATING: 10
Ok, I think it is safe to rate this now.  I have to mention that I worked on this game.  Take that for what it is worth.  I should also mention that of the over 1,500 games I've rated here on the geek, Age of Steam is my favorite game.  

I've played quite a number of expansion maps from the original game so I'm used to how the system is manipulated to greater or lesser effect, but certainly creating different game play.

Well this is more of the same.  I feel that this is just another expansion, with some really fun rules that work toward a greater effect.

Martin took out the only thing that I thought was a flaw in the original game (production) and added a couple great twists (cleaning up bonds and income reduction and adding a money/vp decision). 

The "Basic Game", well, is basic.  I like how the auctions were removed for quick play and ease of learning.  I think it is good for people to have an easier option.  As an expansion, I give it an 8, which is still really a 10 (I rate expansion maps against each other rather than against all other games).  The "Standard Game" is fabu though.  

The Ruhr Valley is a very nice map, it has much of the feel of the original Rust Belt, but works a little better (It doesn't have section that is only viable for late builds the way the Rust Belt does in the midwest).  This can map get tough, I've already see two people almost go bankrupt (myself being one of them).

The NE US map is filled with terrain. It gets really expensive to build. Auctions get high here just to clinch the important efficient/cheaper builds.

All in all fantastic stuff.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Steam is a cut-throat network building game, where players vie to make the best deliveries to make the most profit. The graphical representation is top-notch as cities come in four colours and deliveries are made by taking coloured cubes to a city of the same colour. The length of the route used for a delivery determines how much that delivery is worth in either income or victory points. Take too little income and you might end up bankrupt; take too much income and you can no longer win the game. A turn order mechanism lets players take additional actions, like creating new cities, replenishing the board with extra deliveries, upgrading the range within they can make deliveries etc.

I've played both the basic and the standard game, the latter is my favorite. I don't care much for the turn order auction, but the added upkeep cost for locomotives and the restiction for loans are both great. Both planning and flexibilty become even more crucial.

Owned expansions: Map Expansion #1

RATING: 9.5
Almost a 10, except that I still prefer the original Age of Steam. Playing Steam, though, is a great way to get newbies into the system -- using the Base rules. But rather than play Standard, I'd prefer to just play the original!

Who came up with the "Base" vs. "Standard" nomenclature? I HATE it! They are very different games ... base should be standard, and standard should be auction version (sort of like Tikal)! Gamers don't generally want to play the basic version of anything, and the name "Base" is misleading -- that is the way to play this game, I think!

Base game: Wow! I was not expecting to enjoy this at all, but I am very pleasantly surprised by how well it works! All the roles now have some value throughout the game. The income vs VP decision is interesting -- like other economic euro games, when do you switch from one to the other? The new turn setting mechanism is smooth and makes the game play faster (and should be a LOT easier on AoS newbies). Track building rules are easy to remember, and the double-sided and town tokens work great. Urbanization and goods growth are well-balanced and smoothly integrated, too. And the board and bits are gorgeous! This ought to put Railroad Tycoon away -- this is a much better introduction to the game system!

Standard game: Good, but I prefer the original Age of version -- I LIKE the dice rolls for production! 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I like the changes to the basic game from Age of Steam.  The game is no longer a struggle to survive, but it is still a strategic and tactical challenge against the other players.  I like the way the actions are balanced against your future turn order.  Two of the most annoying aspects of AOS --the possibility of getting into a "dollar auction", and the income reduction, are gone.

RATING: 4

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I had such a different picture in my mind when I imagined this game.  I've always heard that this is the definitive pickup and deliver game.  One that has garnered at least 3 redesigns and a bajillion expansions.  After playing it, I was a little let down.

The game is much simpler than I imagined as well.  Each round players will bid on turn order, then select a special ability, then build tracks, and finally move goods.  The special abilities are things like increasing your track level, placing new cities, building extra lengths of track, etc.  Once each player has built lengths of track they label those lengths with a marker, then they can move goods from one connected city to another matching that good's color.  For each length owned by a player traveled that player earns 1 victory point or 1 point in their income level.

That's it.  There's nothing more to it.  Perhaps the game has been expanded to be more in some of those bajillion expansions but strategies for games this one dimensional are usually pretty simple.  Make as much money as possible early and switch to making points at the right moment.  I found that the game started to get kind of boring 2/3 through my first game.

There is almost no variability or randomness in this game and to that end it felt very solvable.  If playing with a more experienced player you will probably lose just based on the fact that precise strategies and knowledge of the map give a player all the advantages in this game.  One such example is that certain of the special powers are MUCH better than others and not knowing which ones are the best in your first play finds you instantly falling behind.  Also knowing where to build on the map early and how much money in loans to take.  I saw all the experienced players making the same decisions every turn and that's not the kind of game I want to play.  I want to play a game differently every time and explore it.  If I solve a puzzle I don't feel like taking it apart and putting it back together the same way again.

The game doesn't even draw the eye or make you want to pay attention to it.  It's sleepy-looking with muted colors and nondescript wooden cubes and discs.  I'm glad I played it just because of the pedigree but wouldn't seek it out again and it's kind of soured me to vanilla pickup and deliver as well.

RATING: N/A
Great game. I really like it better than Age of Steam. It's more forgiven but it's still a hardcore gamers game. All the choices are there, the production is very good and the time of play is excellent. A good choice for train games.

If Raylroad Tycoon is too much simple and easy to play, Age of Steam too much cruel and hard to manage, Steam is the perfect meeting between both and my favorite train game at this point. I think Martin Wallace really got it right with Steam! Superb game.

Some rules changes made Steam better than Age of Steam IMO. I like the fact that city growing is not a random move that could makes things easier to lucky players. I prefer the kind of game that allows players to chose what they want.

The other rule change I like is the fact that players can't now transport a goods cube that it's not favorable to him, meaning that negative game play is no longer possible by principle. 

The third major change has to do with income and expenses. They both are easier to manage and make the game more friendly.

After a few more plays with only 3 players I'm starting to get a bit tired of the original map and I'm starting to think about new expansions, especially to play with 2/3 players, which is the range I get more often. I understand that this game should be played with more players - minimum four - but I can't gather enough people for that very often so I guess I'll have to go for the small maps expansions.
One of the things that are starting to bug me in Steam is the lack of surprise in the final scoring. I usually lose my games for a couple of points but it's really something I can see a few turns from ending and, in the last couple of games, I couldn't revert the situation. I'm not sure if this means that a good early start makes a too strong position or if it's just a coincidence...

(N)

RATING: 7.5
I don't know what it is about train games, but I suck at them. I guess my head doesn't wrap around the idea of pick-up-and-deliver well yet. In my first play of this lat night, I got buried very early by miscalculating the amount of money I would need to cover my loan payouts + my locomotive upkeep. Huge mistake. There was no hope of me catching up and needless to say, there was no fun to be had as all my efforts were simply to try and keep afloat (in vain).

I know there's a good game here and I want to get it down so I can enjoy it more. I suspect my rating will go up after I grasp the strategies. For now, my only experience was an un-fun one. Keep in mind that I LOVE Brass. It just seems to me like this game system is way more unforgiving than Brass. The loads will break you if you're not careful.

I rate it a 7 after my initial experience. I really hope I enjoy it more with further plays.

RATING: 7.8
3.45
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Much to my surprise, everyone seems to have a strong preference between Age of Steam, Railroad Tycoon, and now Steam. I don't understand it. I've played all three and they're all great games. Actually, to be more accurate, they're all a great game (singular, not plural), with slight variations. These three games are so much more similar than anyone else ever seems to admit. They have a few small differences, but the essence of each game is the same. Some map expansions for Age of Steam change the game far more than either Railroad Tycoon or Steam change the game. To anyone outside the hobby or new to the hobby, the differences between these games (besides the obvious component differences) would be so minuscule as to seem ridiculous that anyone could have a strong preference; it's only from within the hobby that the differences can seem magnified and enormous. I really liked some of the rules tweaks in Steam, and prefer some things in Age of Steam, but they're just variants on the same game in my mind. For instance, I liked the way role selection worked in Steam, but the allocation of deliveries to victory points or income was not an interesting decision as I'd hoped. In the end, I think most people will just prefer whichever game of these three that they tried first, so those who started with Age of Steam will prefer it, but those who started with Steam will likely prefer that one. I started with Age of Steam years ago and have played it 35 times now, so I find myself preferring Age of Steam. If someone only has Railroad Tycoon or only has Steam, I'll gladly play those instead. I thoroughly enjoy expansion maps for Age of Steam, and these two sequels just feel like additional expansion maps with a few rules tweaks like most expansion maps have.

RATING: 5
[thing=27833][/thing] is an economic game abour route building and pick and deliver, coming from the same vein of [thing=4098][/thing] and [thing=17133][/thing], but lighter than the former and heavier than the latter.

[thing=27833][/thing] is drier than [thing=17133][/thing] and has more control. It is certainly better for those looking for a more strategic game, as [thing=27833][/thing] has no random elements once the set up is done, while [thing=17133][/thing] has the events and blind draw of cubes to put in cities. Still, more control doesn't translate to me as more fun, just more mental effort to maximize all actions done, leading to a lot of analisis before each decision, from the choice of the action tile, passing by the placing of rails, and finishing in the delivery of goods.

[thing=27833][/thing] is, therefore, a brain burner of a game, with players thinking about the possible connections, the potential advantages and timming of the action tiles, in the preparation for future deliveries and the development of trains, in the management of money and loans, and in the dispute for paths, cities and resources. Is a game of putting the finger in the eye of others, specially with higher players counts.

However, all this seriousness and complexity also leads the play to resemble too much like a movie session of a bad movie: long periods of silence broken by cursing.

In the end, [thing=27833][/thing] offers a good mental exercize, great to streach the strategy muscles, but I didn't found it particularly interesting for my tastes, nor truly a fun experience of play. I much rather play [thing=17133][/thing] or [thing=31730][/thing].

RATING: 8
Having played both Age Of Steam (2nd ed) and Steam, I find that even the standard version of Steam is more accessible and less unforgiving than AoS is. It is also better looking. But make no mistake – it is still a gamer’s game with many options to consider each turn and a reasonably long playing time. And even though the rules quickly fall into place once you start playing, explaining them to newbies will take some time. All in all, I find that Steam, like AoS, offers a solid track building system with a good amount of turn angst. During my one play with five gamers, however, I did find it a bit abstract – feeling that the streamlining of AoS was done at the expense of the little bit of atmosphere it had. Also, the game peaked around the fifth (out of seven) turns, making the endgame feel a little anti-climactic.

RATING: 5
STANDARD GAME: Unfortunately, there's no way I can comment on this game without comparing it to Age of Steam.  This is obvious, certainly, but not very fair, since I am an Age of Steam junkie.  Steam will never compare well with Age of Steam.  There are some interesting things added to the system (the income track and VP track separation are interesting), other aspects of the system simplified (the cost of building track), and also some much-needed improvements to its pappy (the production rule is nice).  Unfortunately, none of it is anything I really enjoy in comparison.  The income/VP track separation is nice, but it means that you're never truly solvent in the game, since you will need to issue shares at some point in the future, because you can never earn enough money on one turn to pay for all the stuff you likely want to do on a turn; the track cost rules are ... well, actually, there's nothing wrong with that, because simple is always better; the production rule means that goods are even scarcer in Steam than on most Age of Steam maps, and it's not something I'm really wild about, given the way that Steam plays out.  I can't quite put my finger on why I don't like it that well, but it's certainly not that I have some emotional attachment to its pappy (seriously!).  I just find Age of Steam to be the better game between the two.

1 play: 4 players

Rating: 6

-----

BASIC GAME: I figured that, Age of Steam snob that I am, that I wouldn't even want to play this version of the game, but I figured I ought to give it a try, just to be fair.  I liked it more than I expected to, and almost prefer it over the standard game, just because it moved faster, and was over sooner.  It's still Age of Steam, to some extent, but it's much looser, less constrained, and, aside from the track building, a little less competitive.  On the one hand, I figure this could be a good way to introduce folks to the system to move them up toward Age of Steam; on the other hand, you're really not exposing them to the pain that is Age of Steam.  You really have to start with the advanced stuff to get people used to how tight the game is.  I would play this again, but I'm not likely to pick it over Age of Steam.  Ever.

1 play: 3 players
1 play: 5 players

RATING: 10
This game pretty much has it all.  It's a good-looking game, superbly designed and balanced, challenging even for genius board gamers, perfect length, and extremely expandable.  The mechanics are easy enough for veteran gamers to latch onto quickly, yet the number of possible moves in each turn is staggering, making this a brain-burner of the highest order.  But even though this game wears you out, it is fun to play.  You'll re-live your tough losses later as you recall the critical mistakes you made, and you'll also re-live your victories as you recall the good moves that carried you to the win.  You may beat the other players but you don't beat Steam.

RATING: 8
I love the train theme, the track building and the network optimization. The simple economics system is admirable. The dual functions of the action tiles (basic game) are a lovely idea. The art quality varies, but is functional and clear. The color choices of the different playing pieces could be better, especially in less than optimal lightning conditions. I'm not sure I like the random distribution of the deliverable goods, but it wouldn't work as a static version, either. A lack of player interaction usually bothers me, but for some reason, not in Steam. You can sabotage your opponents in subtle ways... Very satisfying to win, and every little mistake will haunt you for a long time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
06/29/09 - After one go, and a previous go at Age of Steam, I feel pretty confident I'm never going to be a fan of this type of game.  By this type, I mean the pickup and delivery of goods type of game.  My train games need a market I can influence, it would seem, in order for them to stick.  This shortcoming, coupled with the fact that I find the need for creative track-building (a boon for some) to be arbitrary and uninteresting, means I won't be lobbying for Steam when the question of what game to play arises.  I do recognize its appeal though, and I'm glad those who weren't ever quite satisfied with either Age of Steam or Railroad Tycoon finally have what appears to be a happy medium.

RATING: 9
蒸汽时代的孪生兄弟，其内容并无多大不同之处，同出自硬派设计师代表马丁之手；美工方面蒸汽相对来说更华丽，同属于铁路经济建设类游戏的代表性作品。对于喜欢网络建设和网络运输方面的桌友来说，蒸汽系列是不二之选。
【关键词】城市化，城市扩张，贷款，火车头升级，维护费，不同地形建筑费用，货物运送及接收城市，得分信贷双轨制

【推荐度】高 【铁路经济运输，中重度德式爱好者
